Yesterday's Grand Opening of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce's National Goods Market

More Than 700 Attendees

A Remarkable Occasion

The National Goods Market, organized by the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce's Products Exhibition Hall, held its grand opening ceremony at 9:00 AM yesterday in the Chamber of Commerce's auditorium. Over 700 representatives from various city organizations and groups attended, making it a truly remarkable occasion. In addition to presenting various national goods on the spot, the "National Products Guide" newspaper also distributed special editions. The details of the event are summarized below:

Opening Ceremony Proceedings

The opening ceremony began at approximately 10:00 AM. After the customary greetings, Chairman Ye Huijun of the Chamber of Commerce delivered a speech outlining the purpose of the event. This was followed by speeches from Vice Minister Zhao of the Ministry of Industry, a representative of the Shanghai Municipal Government, Wang Jiean representing the Jiangsu Chamber of Commerce, and Dong Keren representing the Bureau of Social Affairs. Wang Xiaolai gave a response. After the ceremony concluded, the representatives proceeded to tour the market.

Chairman's Address

Chairman Ye Huijun stated in his address:

"Today, as our Chamber of Commerce's Products Exhibition Hall holds the grand opening ceremony for the National Goods Market, we are deeply honored by the presence and guidance of distinguished guests from all sectors. Our Exhibition Hall was established in the tenth year of the Republic of China [1921] and has been operating for ten years, showcasing the finest national products for public reference. Over these ten years, in addition to hosting six exhibitions and setting up temporary national goods markets, we have been open daily for public viewing. However, considering the recent influx of imported goods and the perceived inferiority of national products, despite the prosperity of Shanghai and the abundance of shops, it is surprisingly difficult to find a place that exclusively sells national goods. This leaves those who wish to support national products without a place to go. Our Chamber of Commerce is responding to the needs of the times, recognizing that the Exhibition Hall should not only serve as a place for viewing but also for purchasing. Therefore, the establishment of the National Goods Market is an urgent necessity for promoting national products. The previous National Industrial and Commercial Conference passed a resolution to encourage the establishment of national goods markets, and national goods exhibition halls in Nanjing and Hangzhou have already established national goods markets. Our Chamber of Commerce is ideally located in a bustling area with numerous shops and a dense population. Therefore, by establishing a National Goods Market with sound organization and diligent management, we can undoubtedly achieve significant business development. This will not only foster a love for national goods among residents but also effectively promote the sales of national products, achieving multiple benefits in one stroke. We believe this is an essential undertaking. The Standing Committee of our Chamber of Commerce resolved to convert one floor of the Exhibition Hall into a permanent National Goods Market before the Tenth Anniversary Exhibition, which will be held during the Double Tenth Festival [October 10th] this year. After three months of preparation, we have finally achieved success. The current market differs from ordinary exhibitions and temporary national goods markets. To ensure the overall quality of the market, we limited each industry to only one participating manufacturer, preventing the inclusion of similar products. We also carefully selected national goods, focusing on aesthetic presentation and arrangement. Participating manufacturers enthusiastically embraced a spirit of sacrifice, not solely for profit. We are grateful to the China General Edison Company for installing electric lights, the Zhenhua Paint Company for painting the cabinets, and the Eastern Lamp Company for decorating with New Year's lanterns. Although we charged a nominal fee to cover costs, the prices were extremely reasonable. We also appreciate the Hongzhang Textile and Dyeing Factory's donation of flag cloth and the generous gifts from various factories for distribution to guests and customers, adding to the enjoyment. These included MSG from Tianchu Flavoring Essence Factory, cigarettes from the Huacheng Tobacco Company, wine from Dykun, and Zhongshan olives from Guanshengyuan. We are deeply grateful for their enthusiastic support. On behalf of the Chamber of Commerce and the National Goods Market, I extend my thanks to everyone. I hope that all participating manufacturers will work together harmoniously, embracing a spirit of collaboration to promote the development of national products. I also hope that all the esteemed guests present today will continue to support us with their patriotic spirit, providing guidance and promoting our efforts. Furthermore, I earnestly hope that the media will actively advocate and publicize our efforts so that our national goods will continue to improve and one day rival those of other countries. I have high expectations."

Speech by Zhao

Vice Minister Zhao Jinqing of the Ministry of Industry stated in his speech: "Today, as the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce's National Goods Market opens, Minister Kong is unable to attend due to official duties and has specifically asked me to represent him. I have one thought to share: the call for promoting national goods did not begin today. In Shanghai alone, there have long been organizations such as the National Goods Maintenance Association, the National Goods Promotion Association, and the National Goods Factories Association, all dedicated to promoting national goods. Temporary markets have also been established in more than one location. Why, then, is it still necessary to promote national goods today? While we cannot blame the people, the underdevelopment of our national goods is a major factor. I will not dwell on other examples, but considering only rice and flour, customs statistics show that we lose approximately 250 million [currency not specified] annually. You can imagine the scale of the problem. I have also repeatedly told my friends in the National Goods Factories Association that we must promote national goods impartially, supporting not only our own products but also those of others. I have seen cases where the products of a national goods factory are excellent, yet the owner's wife and daughters do not use them. This is like going to a Chinese restaurant and ordering oxtail soup. I believe that promoting national goods is not only patriotic and beneficial to others but also ultimately in our own interest. At a time when industry is depressed and production is low, young people often have no way out and resort to suicide. Who doesn't have children? We must plan for their future. The best way to provide them with livelihoods is to vigorously promote production. Promoting production requires a focus on manufacturing national goods. If national goods do not thrive, money will flow out of the country. Money is to a nation as blood is to a body. If the blood dries up, the body will wither. Therefore, we must act before the blood dries up and prevent our nation from perishing." (Other speeches were omitted.)

A Glimpse of the Gifts

On this day, the market pre-issued invitation letters, and each holder of a letter received a bag of national goods. The products and quantities donated by various manufacturers are listed below: Huacheng Tobacco Company: 10,000 cigarettes; China Toothpick Factory: four bundles of toothpicks; Tianchu Flavoring Essence Factory: 1,200 bottles of MSG; French Drugstore: 1,000 packets of Rendan [a traditional Chinese medicine]; Tianran Xianweijing Factory: 20 dozen bottles of Xianweijing sauce; Guanshengyuan: 300 cans of Zhongshan olives and 200 bags of fruit; The Commercial Press: 2,000 portraits of Sun Yat-sen, 1,200 daily and large calendars; Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company: 500 packs of 10 Platinum Dragon cigarettes, 500 packs of 10 Great Wall cigarettes; Paris Cosmetics Factory: 1,000 packs of toothpaste; Family Industrial Cooperative: 1,000 packs of toothpaste; Dykun Company: 500 bottles of wine.

Chen Zuogan, manager of the Lianhua Woolen Mill in Hele Lane, North Henan Road, this city, has always been enthusiastic about the national goods movement. Yesterday, he also transported dozens of the mill's most popular products, including "Three Rings" brand wool swimsuits, hemp swimsuits, sports vests, woolen rope shirts, trousers, men's and women's scarves, woolen socks, and silk stockings, for display to promote the cause.

Yesterday's Anti-Epidemic Campaign

A Grand Parade by Boy Scouts

Yesterday was the day for the Shanghai Municipal Anti-Cholera Campaign's Boy Scout parade, which traveled straight through the Chinese and foreign concessions. The sky was overcast all day, and there was a brief drizzle at 4:35 PM. All the Chinese and foreign Boy Scout troops participating in the city entered the Dalin Road Public Sports Field at 1:25 PM and remained assembled for some time. At that time, Chief Commander Wang Gang and Shen Hao and Wu Liguo from the Health Bureau blew whistles to signal the start of the parade. The scale of the event was unprecedented for an anti-cholera campaign. The events of yesterday are described below:

Officials Present

Officials present at the venue at 0:05 PM yesterday included: Bi Dehui, member of the National Health Administration of the Ministry of the Interior; Hu Hongji, Director of the Municipal Health Bureau; Section Chiefs Shen Hao and Wu Liguo; and over ten staff members. Also present were Wang Gang, Chief Commander of the Boy Scout Troops; Wei Zhiren, Director-General of the French Concession Municipal Council; Pu Bo, Director of the Health Department; Xu Fujun, Chief of the Anti-Epidemic Department; Fei Deng, Director of the Health Department of the Public Concession; Yan Fuqing of the Central University Medical College; and over forty others, who were on-site directing the event.

Number of Troops

Starting at 0:30, Boy Scout troops from various schools successively entered the field and formed ranks. The schools included the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Night School, the Commercial and Industrial Youth Propaganda Corps, Hou Dan, Shizhong, China Women's Physical Education, Patriotic Jinan, Yucai, Southeast, Pudong Middle School, Shangzhong, East Asia, Lizhi, Moore Memorial Church, Chengzhong, Liangjiang, China Physical Education College, Guangzhao Public School, Guangyi, and other Chinese and foreign Boy Scout troops, totaling over 1,200 people. Also present were forty members of the Fifth Detachment of the Public Security Bureau Police and fifteen police officers from the Second District Police Department.

Inside the sports field, Boy Scout troops from various schools were led by commanders into designated areas. After a while, the perimeter of the field was packed with spectators. Fortunately, there was no scorching sun, so the officials on-site were able to proceed smoothly with their tasks. Various models, such as a paper coffin with no bottom, inscribed with red and white anti-cholera warnings conveying common sense, buckets of sewage, paper boats, fruit baskets, and night soil buckets, all had large signs. Unclean food and utensils were covered with flies. There were also six oversized artificial flies. The Public and French Concessions had made fifty loudspeakers, dozens of large banners with slogans, and several health warning signs. In particular, the sickbed team and the thirty-odd simulated male and female cholera patients, placed on canvas stretchers, were a shocking reminder of battlefield casualties. Other items were too numerous to mention.

Departure

When the parade set off from the Public Sports Field, sixteen traffic police officers on bicycles led the way, followed by the Chief Commander's car. The Shanghai Middle School band led the first team, and the music filled the air, creating a tense atmosphere. Fifty-two Boy Scout troops moved in an orderly and uniform manner. As the teams reached the middle section of Dalin Road, the sidewalks were packed with spectators, making it almost impossible to pass. Fortunately, the traffic police were able to maintain order about five or six yards ahead, minimizing congestion.

Parade Overview

The procession snaked its way to Avenue Foch near the Great World amusement center, where the crowds were extremely dense. The Great World's western-facing floors were filled with spectators watching the parade on the street. Public buses and trolley buses were temporarily suspended. At 3:10 PM, the procession reached the intersection of Tibet Road and Nanking Road. At 4:05 PM, the procession reached Avenue Albert, and at 5:15 PM, it reached the middle section of Baoshan Road. At this time, there was a light drizzle.

Page 14

The teams maintained their spirit and showed little sign of fatigue. The rain soon stopped, and at 6:20 PM, the procession arrived at the end of North Sichuan Road. Along the way, the teams shouted anti-cholera slogans in unison. The most amusing team was the sewage team. At the front was a paper boat carried by four people. Two students from the East Asia Physical Education College, dressed as boatmen, wore white towels around their heads, were about 27 years old, and wore blue cloth shirts and trousers. They applied white powder to their faces and carried chamber pots and scrub brushes, one holding a bundle of greens. They grimaced and shouted, "This man took a great risk, drinking raw water and sewage. He got cholera!" They would then point to the sickbed behind the boat with a simulated dead person and shout, "Everyone, look! He died from drinking unclean water!" They repeated this at every location, to the applause of the audience. The coffin team and the health team were also well-organized. Chinese and foreign Boy Scouts distributed leaflets. Injection vehicles provided by the concession authorities and the Health Bureau passed through the area, encouraging spectators to get cholera vaccinations. When the parade reached the end of North Sichuan Road at the intersection of Tientung'an Road, the over one thousand Chinese and foreign Boy Scouts were transported back to their schools by waiting trucks.

Girl Scouts Carrying a Large Fly in the Parade

(Photo by this newspaper)

Roadside Protection

Yesterday afternoon, the parade traveled over ten li [approximately 3 miles] through the Chinese and foreign concessions. There were no incidents. Fifty-five members of the Public Security Bureau's detachment and police officers maintained order along the route. At the junction of Avenue des Cerisiers and the French Concession, the police team handed over the flag to French Concession police officers. At the junction of Avenue Foch and Tibet Road, the guards of the Public Concession were exchanged. From the start to the destination, the order was well maintained.

Parade Notes

Yesterday, the officials of the Health Bureau and Chief Commander Wang Gang all skipped lunch. They rushed to the sports field after 10:00 AM and were busy. The Youlian Film Company sent people to film at the venue and along the route. The photographers ran around, sweating profusely, trying to capture everything. The Lever Brothers Soap Factory, a foreign company, provided a large car to distribute advertising leaflets and shouted to buy Lever disinfectant soap.

Xiong Shihui's Talk

Returned to Shanghai Yesterday Morning Specifically to Dispel Rumors

Total Elimination of Communist Bandits Within One Month

Xiong Shihui, Garrison Commander of Shanghai and Songhu, returned to Shanghai yesterday morning at 7:00 AM on the overnight express train from Nanjing after being summoned to the capital by Chairman Chiang for important consultations. A reporter from this newspaper interviewed him at his residence. Xiong's foot ailment has fully recovered, and he is in high spirits. His remarks are recorded below: Construction Plans Xiong stated that regarding the central government's recent measures and the political situation, there are four points worth reporting: (1) The central government is continuing to vigorously pursue construction projects according to the original plan and is intensifying its efforts, without delaying due to other factors. The Supreme Economic Council will be established soon to plan economic construction, and the diplomatic policy will also proceed according to a fixed procedure.

Guangdong Incident (2) The internal elements of the Guangdong issue are politically complex, even more so than the Enlarged Conference. From a scientific standpoint, it is impossible to combine incompatible elements in one place and expect them to harmonize. Recent divisions indicate impending defeat. In terms of military strength, they are nothing more than a few divisions and cannot resist the central government. In the eyes of informed observers, the Guangdong side's actions are childish. The central government has adopted a policy of non-interference, allowing them to survive or perish on their own. Total Elimination of Communist Bandits (3) The central government believes that the biggest hidden danger is the Communist bandits. Therefore, it has resolved to completely eliminate them, using the national force to concentrate on Jiangxi Province, giving a deadline of one month for complete elimination, with a maximum of two months. Chairman Chiang has decided to personally go to Jiangxi to supervise the suppression.

Situation in North China (4) Regarding the situation in North China, the northern generals all obey the central government's orders. Rumors are unbelievable. In the current situation, Yan and Feng no longer have the ability to command their subordinates. The recent telegrams from northern generals denouncing Gu Chenhao for creating chaos further prove that there is nothing to worry about. Vice Commander Zhang is suffering from the flu. Mayor Zhang has repeatedly telegraphed, saying that he will be discharged in about one to two weeks. Xiong then said that he heard rumors in Nanjing about malicious people spreading rumors in Shanghai. Therefore, he returned to Shanghai to inspect the situation. He will still need to go to Nanjing in the next few days to meet with Chairman Chiang to discuss the elimination of the Communist bandits.

The Jiangxi Disaster Relief Association

Held a Reception for the Press to Report on the Disaster Situation

With a Goal of 500,000 [Currency not Specified]

The areas where the bandit disaster has not subsided have not yet been surveyed. In total, about 70 of the province's 81 counties are devastated. The severity of the disaster is unprecedented. It is requested that the media unanimously support and widely publicize the situation. Reporters then visited Xiong Shihui at his residence. The Ministry of Industry Denies Duty-Free Import of Cuban Sugar

Encouraging Sugar Merchants to Think Fundamentally

The local Sugar Trade Association previously reported that a large quantity of Cuban sugar would be imported into China duty-free and sold at low prices, causing a significant impact. The association telegraphed the various departments of the National Government, requesting assistance. Yesterday, the association received a reply from the Ministry of Industry, stating: "Received your telegram. Upon investigation, China's annual imports of foreign sugar are valued at around 100 million [currency not specified], ranking second among all imported goods subject to tariffs. It is imperative to seek self-sufficiency in sugar to close the loopholes. Therefore, it is necessary to refine crude sugar to meet immediate needs and cultivate raw materials to strengthen the foundation. The Fourth Plenary Session of the last year had a resolution on this matter. The Ministry is now developing a comprehensive sugar industry plan to gradually implement this resolution. As for the submitted sections, after investigation, the domestic sugar production has been decreasing in recent years. Before the Republic, Shanghai sold over one million dan [approximately 110,231 lbs] annually. Last year, it had decreased to 50,000 dan. The government is deeply concerned about this situation and should take measures to support the development of the industry at any time. The association's claim that the import of Cuban sugar was approved by the government with duty-free imports is absolutely untrue and should not be a concern. The current difficulties faced by sugar merchants, claiming to be affected by the high value of gold and the low value of silver, are a separate issue. The Ministry has not heard of Cuban sugar being sold at particularly low prices. In general, the sugar merchants of the association have a patriotic heart. During this period, they should think fundamentally, improve technology extensively, reduce costs, and provide a large quantity of raw sugar to assist the government in developing the refined sugar industry, so that the domestic sugar industry can gradually make progress."

Local News Two

Five Kidnappers in the Li Guoliang Case Executed by Firing Squad

Xu Jiajun Died Without Regret

Li Shaoxuan Asked His Wife to Collect His Body

Chen Zhenzhi Sang Erhuang Opera On the Spot

Wei Huizhang Wrote Characters in Court

Zhang Kun Missed His Wife and Mother

Xu Jiajun, from Yunnan, was related to Li Guoliang, the owner of the Xingli Copper and Tin Shop at 515 Zhejiang Road. Knowing that Li was well-off, he conspired with Li Shaoxuan (also known as Yang Nanxuan) from Sichuan, Chen Zhenzhi (also known as Xia Jizhi) from Hubei, Zhang Kun, and Wei Huizhang from Danyang to kidnap Li on the evening of November 28 last year and demand a huge ransom. The case was solved by the Lao Zha Police Station and sent to the Special District Local Court for trial. Xu, Li, Chen, Zhang, and Wei were each sentenced to death. The Special Court submitted the case to the higher authorities, and the order was issued to execute the death penalty by firing squad. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Cheng Shangfeng instructed the police station to send detectives to the West Prison to interrogate the five criminals and ask if they had any last words. Xu Jiajun said, "I am 33 years old this year, and I die without regret. I have already written and sent a letter to my family from prison. However, I still have 500 [currency not specified] deposited with Sun Zhongweng at the Heshengji Pawnshop in Gongshun Lane, Wuma Road. Please inform them to return the money to my family to support my children." Li Shaoxuan said, "I am 32 years old. Please write a letter to my wife, Huang Abao, at 36 Ximen Road, to collect my body and retrieve my deposit of six yuan [currency not specified] from the police station to buy ingots to burn for me." Chen said, "I am 26 years old. Today, I am finally freed from suffering and have no regrets." Wei said, "I am 30 years old. Please give me paper and pen so I can write characters on the spot to leave as a souvenir." The characters he wrote were incoherent and unintelligible. Zhang said, "I am 24 years old. Please send the lined spring leather robe that I have stored in prison to the Zhang Xingtai Dye Shop in Xujiawan to be given to my father." After the interrogation, they were given wine and food as usual, then escorted onto prisoner trucks and taken to the execution ground at the Second Jiangsu Prison in Caohejing. The Local Court appointed Prosecutor Wang Sixian as the execution officer. Police Chief Xu Jinqing and police officer Chen [name illegible] assembled the execution police officers Wang Jianqing, Gu Hanqing, Zhu Wanyuan, Xue Bingzhang, Li Zuoqing, Zou Zhen dong, and Zhang Chunshen, who brought the criminals forward. Xu Jiajun said, "I am 33 years old, from Yunnan. My mother is at home, and I have no last words." Li Shaoxuan said, "I am 32 years old, from Sichuan. My mother is in my hometown. I ask that two pieces of clothing be kept for my mother to claim when she comes to see her son's face." Chen Zhenzhi said, "I am 26 years old, from Hubei. I have no last words." He then sang Erhuang opera loudly in front of the court. Wei Huizhang said, "I am 30 years old, from Danyang. I regret that I want to write a letter but have nowhere to send it." Zhang Kun said, "I am 24 years old, from Hubei. I have a wife, children, and an elderly mother at home. Tell them to live well." At this point, the execution order was carried out. Under the command of Police Chief Xu, the execution police officers executed the criminals by firing squad. The bodies were taken away by the court for burial.

Horse Songting Executed by Strangulation for Strangling His Paramour

Sending a Letter to His Brother to Entrust His Orphaned Child

Breaking Out in a Loud Cursing of His Paramour

Ma Songting from Suqian previously lured Song Qiaobao, a young widow, from Suzhou to Shanghai and lived with her as his paramour. On the morning of February 13th of last year, Ma suddenly conceived a plan to kill her for her money. He strangled the woman to death at their residence at 373 Hejian Road, then robbed her of her gold jewelry and cash, and fled. This spring, he was apprehended by the police in Nanjing. Detectives were dispatched by the Shanghai police to escort him back to Shanghai, where he was tried and sentenced to death by the Special District Local Court. Yesterday afternoon, the execution by strangulation was carried out. Judge Cheng brought Ma to court for questioning. According to his confession, he had a son named Shengxing who should be entrusted to his brother Ma Shouting and his sister-in-law for upbringing. He had nothing else to say. Judge Cheng then offered him food and wine. After he finished eating, he was ordered to be escorted into a prison van and taken to the Caohejing Jiangsu Second Prison execution ground. Wang Enxian, a prosecutor from the Local Court, was appointed as the supervising officer of the execution. He immediately ordered Police Chief Xu Jinqing and Police Officer Chen Xihui to accompany the executioners Zhu Wanwan, Wang Jianqing, and Zou Zhendong to Caohejing Jiangsu Second Prison. The judge, along with Warden Dong, took their seats. The prisoner was brought in and questioned again. The prisoner requested to write a letter to his brother Ma Shouting at Xiangyan Bridge, informing him that he had been executed. He then broke out in a loud cursing of Song Qiaobao. The judge ordered the execution to proceed. Police Chief Xu and Police Officer Chen, in collaboration with the executioners, bound the prisoner to the stake in accordance with the law and slowly strangled him with a rope. He soon stopped breathing. After the coroner confirmed his death, the judge ordered the strangulation stake to be sealed and preserved for a re-examination on a later date, before the body was taken for burial.

Silk Merchant Zhu Ligeng Identifies Kidnapping Bandits

Zhang Debiao Once Brandished a Gun, Threatening

Hao Zifeng Seized the Bodyguard's Gun

The Two Bandits Were Speechless After Being Identified

Wang Zhenhuan, the owner of the Wang Yutai Tea Shop, was previously kidnapped by bandits on Julai Road in the French Concession. During the pursuit of the kidnappers, Chinese Constable No. 2124 of the New Gate Police Station in the Public Concession was shot and killed by the bandits while resisting arrest. Recently, the French police apprehended the male and female bandits Zhang Debiao and Hao Zifeng, along with their paramours Hao Su and Zhang Shen, and handed them over to the French Concession Court. Zhang and Hao were each sentenced to five years in the Western Prison, and the two women were each sentenced to one year. It is now learned that the police authorities of the Public Concession suspected that the bandits were responsible for the shooting death of Chinese Constable No. 2124. Therefore, Chinese Detective Chief Lu Liankui and Detective Officers Tang Jian and Wang Chengying specially brought the four bandits back to the General Police Station for investigation. The four bandits vehemently denied shooting the Chinese Constable. However, Zhang Debiao confessed that on the morning of April 4th at 8:00 AM, he had conspired with three accomplices to kidnap Zhu Ligeng, a merchant from Haimen, on Changsha Road, but failed. Zhu is currently 42 years old, resides at No. 215 Changsha Road, and owns the Zhongfu Silk Factory in Zhabei. He usually travels in a No. 10320 car and employs a bodyguard, Wang Xueren. That morning, Zhu and Wang were about to board the car in front of their residence when four bandits suddenly rushed out from the side of the road. One prevented the driver, Chen Xiangyun, from driving, one boarded Zhu's car intending to seize the bodyguard's weapon, and another held a handgun to prevent Zhu from shouting. Fortunately, Wang Xue was alert and took the opportunity to get out of the car and run quickly into a nearby alley. One bandit immediately chased after Wang, who then fired a gun at the bandit. The bandits, realizing that they were prepared and that it would be difficult to succeed, fled in a panic. Zhu was thus spared from becoming a "wealth god." Later, based on intelligence reports, the police learned that Zhang's confession implicated the other men and women. Zhu, his bodyguard, and the driver were summoned to the police station. Zhang and Hao were mixed among a group of other criminals, and Zhu was asked to identify them. Zhu identified Zhang Debiao as the bandit who had pointed a gun at him and prevented him from shouting, and Wang Xueren also identified Hao as the bandit who had tried to seize his gun. Thereupon, the two bandits lowered their heads in silence. Subsequently, the bandits' women, Zhang Shen and Hao Su, further confessed that four or five days before the attempted kidnapping of Zhu, they had delivered a handgun to the Xieji Hotel on Hankou Road to Zhang. Yesterday morning, the police sent the four men and women to the Special District Local Court to report the details of the case. Zhu and his driver also appeared in court to testify. Judge Ge questioned the four bandits and ordered them to be detained separately for a subsequent hearing.

Son-in-Law Xue Files Suit to Claim His Children's Share of Maternal Grandfather's Estate

Temporarily Calculated at 200,000 Yuan

Trial Postponed Due to Unpaid Court Fees

After the death of Xue Baorun, a prominent dye merchant, his wives and children engaged in lawsuits to contest his estate, which have continued unabated. The family members have become enemies. For the past six months, reports about the Xue family's estate battle have repeatedly appeared in newspapers. Now, Hua Lihou, Hua Yigu, and Hua Manyun, father and children, have jointly filed a lawsuit, requesting the court to order Xue Sun, Xue Yisheng, Xue Yansheng, Xue Jiasheng, and Xue Gensheng to hand over the entire estate for distribution. Xue Baorun had a total of seven children. The defendants in this case, with the exception of Xue Sun, are all sons of Baorun. There are also three daughters named Xue Qin舫, Xue Chaoqun, and Xue Baobao. Qin舫 married Hua Lihou in the 34th year of the Guangxu reign (Qing Dynasty) and had two sons, Hua Yihong and Hua Yigu, and a daughter, Manyun. Qin舫 passed away in 1919. Now, because Yigu and Manyun are minors, this legal action to claim a share of their maternal grandfather's estate is being pursued by their father, Hua Lihou, as their legal guardian. Although this case appears to be a dispute between nephews/nieces and their maternal grandmother and uncles, it is in reality a conflict between a son-in-law and his mother-in-law and brothers-in-law. Since the enactment of laws granting women the right to inherit their parents' estate, the number of estate division lawsuits has greatly increased. However, it is rare to see a case where, after a daughter's death, her son-in-law and nephews/nieces are fighting for a share of the in-laws' estate. This case appears to be the first of its kind. An excerpt of the plaintiffs' complaint is provided below:

(Omitted above) After the death of our maternal grandfather, the defendants petitioned this court for a certificate to manage the estate. However, after the defendants began managing the estate, they only knew how to waste it and failed to divide it according to the law. We have repeatedly urged them to distribute our rightful share, but the defendants, intending to embezzle the estate, have repeatedly refused. An interpretation by the Judicial Yuan has confirmed that grandchildren can inherit by substitution. Specifically, Order No. 405 of the Judicial Yuan, dated January 19, 1931, stated that after receiving a request from the Shanghai Bar Association to interpret ambiguities regarding a married woman's inheritance rights, the request was forwarded to the Supreme Court, which stated that since men and women should have equal property inheritance rights, if a married woman who legally has the right to inherit property has already passed away before the commencement of the inheritance, the property that the woman should have inherited should be inherited by her direct lineal descendants. Furthermore, regardless of whether a woman is married or unmarried, if she has the right to inherit property, then she should be jointly responsible with her brothers for her parents' debts if her estate is insufficient to cover them and there is no limited inheritance. If her parents have no other children, then she should be solely responsible for repaying the debts. Furthermore, current law does not grant women the right to inherit ancestral property, so they cannot claim to manage, divide, or receive interest from property used for ancestral worship. Order No. 424 of the Judicial Yuan, dated February 2, 1931, stated that after receiving a request from the Shanghai Bar Association to interpret ambiguities regarding a married woman's inheritance rights, the request was forwarded to the Supreme Court, which stated that if a married woman with the right to inherit property dies before the commencement of the inheritance, her share should be inherited by her children by substitution. However, if the property that she should have inherited has already been divided by other heirs before the implementation of the Detailed Rules for Retrospective Inheritance of Property by Married Women, attention should be paid to the provisions of Article 3, Paragraph 2 of the Detailed Rules. The defendants have dared to disregard national laws, seized the estate, and intend to embezzle it, which is extremely illegal. Therefore, we file this lawsuit. Because the entire estate has been seized, we cannot determine its exact value. One-sixth of it is temporarily calculated at 200,000 yuan. We also declare...

Yesterday morning, Judge Zhou Daren of the Special District Local Court opened the Ninth Civil Court to hear the case. The plaintiffs' lawyers, Yang Linzhi, Zhang Jiahui, and Ye Shaoying, and the defendant Xue Yansheng's lawyers, Lin Yingqing and Wang Zijian, all appeared in court to argue their cases. Judge Zhou stated that since the plaintiffs had estimated the value of the subject of the lawsuit to be 200,000 yuan and had not yet paid the required court fees, the court could not proceed with the trial. He ordered the trial to be postponed until the court fees were paid.

Sheng Yuyou Accuses Cousin of Stealing 100,000 Yuan in Savings

When His Stepmother Sheng Gong Passed Away

Her Nephew Took the Opportunity to Steal

Sheng Yuyou, the grandson of Sheng Xingxun, a former palace guardian of the Qing Dynasty, currently residing at 526 Jing'an Temple Road, recently hired lawyer Jiang Yiping to accuse his stepmother Sheng Gong's nephew, Mao Zengnian (also known as Mao Dongsheng), of theft in the Special District Court. The complaint alleges that Mao Zengnian, the nephew of the plaintiff's stepmother Sheng Gong, has been residing at 526 Sheng Residence, Jing'an Temple Road. On the afternoon of the 18th of this month at 8:00 PM, the plaintiff's stepmother passed away. The defendant, taking advantage of the absence of Sheng's family members, secretly stole Gong's savings deposit books from the Four Ming Bank and Shanghai Bank, Kadlu Branch, and Wuzhen, totaling 100,000 yuan, along with a set of seals. Afterwards, an investigation was conducted at various banks, and it was discovered that the defendant had already withdrawn a portion of Gong's savings from the Shanghai Bank, totaling 20,000 taels of silver, and had disappeared without a trace. The plaintiff is the adopted son of the third branch of the Sheng family and, according to law, should have the right to inherit his stepmother Sheng Gong's estate. The defendant's actions clearly violate the criminal law. In addition to reporting the case to the police, this complaint is filed requesting that the defendant be investigated and prosecuted according to the law, along with a civil lawsuit and a request to instruct the aforementioned banks to prohibit the defendant from withdrawing any deposits under Sheng Gong's Wuzhen account to prevent further losses. It is reported that the court has received the complaint and will soon summon both parties to appear in court for a hearing.

Request to Ban Gambling in Amusement Parks

The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers' Association sent a letter to the Municipal Council yesterday, stating: "Dear Sirs, We are writing to you in response to a letter from Mr. Zhu Rongping, who stated that gambling is a major scourge on public morals and fraud is intolerable under national law. The happiness of the people and the stability of society are all related to this issue. Therefore, dog racing and roulette are prohibited by law. However, activities similar to these are still rampant, harming the ignorant masses. It has been found that the rooftop gardens of the Wing On, Sincere, and Sun Sun department stores, as well as the New World amusement park, all have gambling-like activities, such as winning prizes by ringing bells, obtaining cigarettes through roulette, and profiting from ring toss games. In terms of their content, all of them involve fraudulent activities. The so-called "winning prizes by ringing bells" never offers any large prizes. The attempt to make a profit from ring toss games always involves deceiving the ignorant masses through unclear pricing and the convenient pursuit of profit. If questioned, they resort to beatings, stripping of clothes, and other evil acts. As for roulette for cigarettes, regardless of what is being gambled, it is fundamentally a violation of the law. Therefore, ignorant people who enter these places are bound to be swindled. Therefore, we are writing to request that your council investigate this fraudulent situation and ban these activities, so that visitors will no longer be deceived and your council's commitment to banning gambling will be fully implemented. The benefits of this would be immense." The association believes that the contents of the letter are insightful and related to the harmfulness of gambling. Therefore, we are writing to request that your Bureau investigate and prohibit these activities.

Soochow University Invites Ms. Liu Manqing to Lecture

Soochow University in Shanghai has always paid close attention to the issue of China's border regions. It has established a Border Studies Association to study all aspects of the border regions. The university recently heard that Ms. Liu Manqing, who traveled to Tibet alone two years ago to conduct research, had recently come to Shanghai. They specially asked Mr. Huang Jingwan of the Commercial Press to introduce her. Yesterday morning at 11:00 AM, she came to the university to lecture. Also in attendance were Gesang Zeren, a special commissioner of the Sichuan-Xikang Party Affairs, Yang Zhonghua, an aide, Huang Ziyi, and Ms. Liu Manqing's sister, Ms. Liu Manyun. President Liu Zhanen of the university extended a warm welcome and gathered all 800 male and female students in the auditorium to listen to Ms. Liu's lecture. Ms. Liu calmly took the stage and said, "I was born on the border and have limited knowledge. I feel both ashamed and honored to be invited by Shanghai's highest institution of learning to give a lecture. The issue of the border regions has long been neglected by the Chinese people. In addition, for the past ten years or so, the government and scholars have been out of touch with Tibet, and the situation has become even more isolated. Two years ago, I was ordered to go to Tibet to conduct research. This was a rash undertaking. The climate in Tibet is extremely cold, the mountain passes are covered in snow that is several meters deep, the roads are rugged, and bandits are everywhere. The hardships I experienced are beyond description. However, because I was on a mission, I did not dare to give up despite the setbacks. Fortunately, I managed to reach Lhasa and meet with the Dalai Lama to convey the central government's intentions. The result was satisfactory. The Dalai Lama, who had been out of touch with the government for more than ten years, has now sent a plenipotentiary representative to reside permanently in Beijing. In the future, relations between China and Tibet will gradually become closer. All I have contributed in recent years is this. I hope that you will be able to conduct more solid, on-the-ground research on Tibet in the future. With your vast knowledge, you will surely achieve more and contribute more to the border regions. This is my hope." Next, Mr. Gesang Zeren gave a speech, saying, "China's inland areas are densely populated. Young people with ambitions and knowledge have no way out. Xikang and Tibet, on the other hand, are vast and sparsely populated, with abundant treasures. However, due to the lack of talent, no one is developing them, and they will inevitably remain remote and desolate areas. Your university's insight is commendable, and your establishment of the Border Studies Association to engage in exploration is admirable. I hope that in the future, your slogan will be 'Go to the border regions,' because going to the border regions is the only true way out for us. I have been in the inland for three years and have made no contributions to my hometown. I am deeply ashamed of this. I have now been ordered by the central government to return to Xikang to handle party affairs and to inspect the political and cultural situation. In Xikang, in addition to promoting party principles, I also intend to work hard on cultural undertakings. I hope that in the near future, you will come to my humble and remote land. I will welcome you wholeheartedly. When I return to Xikang, I also intend to select students from various places and send them to the inland to study at your university. I hope you will provide guidance." After Mr. Gesang's speech, President Liu invited Mr. Fu, an American sociologist, to give a speech. Mr. Fu also came to meet Ms. Liu because of her lecture at the university. After the meeting, President Liu hosted a luncheon at his residence. Mr. Fu and Mr. Huang Jingwan were also in attendance. Mr. Fu heard that Ms. Liu had written a book about her journey to Tibet, "Kangzang Zhaozheng," which will soon be published by the Commercial Press, and he greatly admired it. He plans to translate it into English for people in his country to read. At the same time, many students at the university asked Mr. Gesang and Ms. Liu to sign autographs as souvenirs, and President Liu and his wife especially entertained them and said that if students from Xikang wanted to study at the university, they would be given free preferential treatment and assistance.

Shanghai to Have a Very Large Swimming Pool

A Beauty Contest to Be Held

Since the Ming Garden closed, it has been reorganized into a large amusement park. The interior work is extremely busy. A canopy eighty feet high has been built to accommodate a thousand workers who are building the swimming pool day and night. The design of this swimming pool is scientific, hygienic, and extremely safe. The pool area is about two hundred feet long and just under one hundred and twenty feet wide. The shallow end is only two feet deep for children to swim in, and the deep end is thirteen feet deep. It has a storage capacity of one million gallons of water. The pool water is changed frequently, and it is stipulated that every two hours it must undergo a scientific sterilization process. Every morning, the pool will be cleaned and wiped, and then the water will be refilled. Water samples will be tested regularly to ensure that there are no toxins that could harm the human body or skin. The park has one thousand shower rooms with one hundred hot and cold water faucets. All kinds of diving boards, water slides, swimming rings, and large rubber rings for children to float on are readily available. There are also various new and beautiful bathing suits for rent. The shallow water beach is covered with white sand, and the beach is equipped with colorful large parasols and tea tables. There is also a radio station that broadcasts music day and night. At the same time, there are plans to hold an unprecedented international beauty contest. The contest is scheduled to begin in August or September. This contest will be guaranteed by Shanghai's socialite charitable organizations. A percentage of the ticket revenue will be used for charitable purposes. The contest will be held in two stages. The first stage will be a contest for women from Russia, France, Germany, and England. The second stage, in August, will be a contest for Chinese women. In the third and final stage, the beauty queens selected in the previous stages will compete in a final election. The judges will select the most beautiful woman, who will be crowned Miss Seas and given the title of "Beautiful Queen," and the committee will award her a beautiful gift. This beauty contest and other novel entertainment activities that Shanghai has never seen before will be held at the Ming Garden this summer. The opening date is in July, and it will surely draw crowds from all over Shanghai.

Water Supply Dispute in Nanshun Jinli, Feihong Road, Zhabei

Authorities Order Owners to Connect to Tap Water

Residents of Nanshun Jinli, Feihong Road, Zhabei, mainly rely on well water

Page 16

There are three sets of public taps, but the water flow is not smooth. Most of the residents are working class, and more than ten people often draw water at the same time. The taps are too few to meet the demand, and disputes often arise. The Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, after receiving a report, ordered the owner, Chen Yelan, to add more taps or connect to Zhabei tap water to facilitate drinking water. Subsequently, Chen Yelan replied that Nos. 1 to 34 of the alley belong to the three owners Kang Shaonian, Shi Gan, and Gu Hu, and only Nos. 35 to 71 belong to Chen. The original three taps are sufficient for his own use, but because the properties of Kang and others do not have water supply facilities, they also pay a fee to use the taps, resulting in a shortage. The Bureau considered this a violation of the water supply rules, which state that owners who have their own water supply cannot supply water to properties outside their own. Chen was ordered to stop supplying well water to residents outside his own properties, and Kang, Shi, and Hu were strictly ordered to connect to tap water before the 15th of this month to supply drinking water to the residents of their own properties. A notice was also issued to the residents of Nos. 1 to 34 stating that if the owners fail to comply by the deadline, the residents can apply to the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company for tap water on their own, and all expenses will be deducted from their rent.

Joint Meeting of the Supervisory and Executive Committees of the Jisheng Society

Report on Disaster Relief Efforts in Nine Provinces This Year

The China Jisheng Society in Shanghai held a joint meeting of the Supervisory and Executive Committees the day before yesterday to discuss disaster relief efforts in the nine provinces of Jiangxi, Shaanxi, Hebei, Liaoning, Rehe, Anhui, Henan, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang. Chairman Wang Yiting attended on behalf of the Society, with Vice-Chairman Huang Hanzhi substituting. More than 20 people attended the meeting, including Vice-Chairman Huang, Vice-Chairman Xu Qianlin, and committee members Qu Junwen and Zhang Junxianqing. Reports were given on the current situation of disaster relief, which are summarized below: (1) Committee Member Zhang Xianqing reported on disaster relief efforts in Nanchang and other counties in Jiangxi Province. The Society is jointly running the Nanchang Refugee Shelter and the Ji'an Refugee Shelter with the Morality Society. The two societies have previously allocated 3,000 yuan to the Nanchang shelter and 4,000 yuan to the Ji'an shelter. Another 4,000 yuan has been allocated, as well as more than 2,980 yuan for emergency relief and 5,000 yuan for disaster relief in Guangchang, more than 5,200 sets of cotton clothes worth more than 11,000 yuan, and other disaster relief expenses totaling more than 30,000 yuan. (2) A disaster relief director stated that the Zhejiang Ninghai Dike Gate project is continuing. The original project of building 70-odd dikes in Youdu, Zhongdu, and Xuepo villages is nearing completion. Recently, Mr. Ye Shenzibu of Ninghai proposed to add three dikes connected to the village, namely Chuandong, Xinpingyan, and Laopingyan, to complete the project. In addition to raising funds locally, there is still a shortage of 14,000 yuan. This meeting will consider ways to make up the difference. A letter has also been received from Mr. Sun Yinting, who stated that the local people have requested the repair of dikes in Xiaojian Village and other places in Maolin District. This project is very important and requires 6,200 yuan. The Society, considering the long-term importance of water conservancy, consulted with Vice-Chairman Huang Hanzhi and Committee Member Qu Wenliu and decided to raise funds to assist. The funds have been transferred to the project's disaster relief director, Yinting, to proceed. (3) Committee Member Qu Wenliu stated that the three bridges in Linhai, Zhejiang, namely the Qiaogong Bridge, the Xidong Bridge, and the Yangdu Bridge, have now been completed. After the construction of these three bridges, the local people were inspired to build more than a dozen bridges, all in the name of the Jisheng Society. The Society paid for the labor costs, and the materials were donated locally. Therefore, the Society's investment of 40,000 yuan was equivalent to 100,000 yuan in materials and labor. Zhongdu Bridge is larger, and Mr. Li Yunmen initially tried to build it, but construction was halted due to the difficulty of driving piles. If the weather is favorable and the procedures are legal, 40,000 yuan would be enough to complete it. Funds are now available, but only 15,000 yuan, leaving a shortage of 30,000 yuan. Due to the difficulty of working in the water, the project will be delayed until the second half of the year, but the goal is to complete it. (4) A disaster relief director also went to Shaanxi for disaster relief. Last year, a total of 437,000 yuan was disbursed. This year, Mr. Li Yunmen went to investigate and continue disaster relief in Wugong, running four porridge kitchens, two disaster orphan shelters, and providing seeds, burying corpses, and emergency relief in Liquan, Qianxian, Jingyang, and Lanzhou counties, totaling about 117,000 yuan. Together with the various disaster relief funds mentioned above, the total amount used is about 550,000 to 600,000 yuan. (5) It was also stated that the Society runs three porridge kitchens in Beiping: Baiyian, Landianchang, and Sanshucun. Emergency relief in Xuanhua has been increased from 10,000 yuan to 17,000 yuan. From January 1st to May 30th of this year, a total of more than 37,000 yuan has been allocated for porridge kitchens and emergency relief, and more than 15,000 sets of disaster relief clothing have been provided. The Society's increased disaster relief in Xuanhua has also extended the county's porridge kitchens for three months. (6) In Suizhong, Liaoning Province, the Society runs three porridge kitchens in Xiaozhuangzi, Daquezhuangzi, and Dawangzhuangzi, using a total of more than 25,200 yuan for disaster relief. An additional 15,000 yuan was allocated for dry food. Mr. Yang Zigong, chairman of the charity associations in the four provinces of Rehe, Fengtian, Jilin, and Heilongjiang, allocated 5,000 yuan in the Society's name for disaster relief grain, totaling 20,000 yuan. 11,000 sets of cotton clothes were also provided. (7) Five porridge kitchens are planned for the Chaoyang porridge kitchen in Rehe. The Society allocated 10,000 yuan, and Zhu Zila allocated 10,000 yuan. The project is currently underway. However, the disaster is severe, and 5,000 yuan must be added to each kitchen to sustain them. (8) In Liuan, Anhui, the Society's Mr. Feng Yangshan and Mr. Zepu went there and distributed emergency relief funds in two installments over the past two years, totaling more than 30,000 yuan, including disaster relief expenses. The report has now been filed. (9) The Yangli River project in Henan Province was started last year, but the work was less than halfway done due to military interference. Now, it cannot proceed because of the flood, and the Society's finances are strained. It can only be discussed again next spring, depending on the financial situation. The bridge and gate projects in the county are urgent. The Nanyang Jisheng Branch has asked engineer Xu to handle it. The original estimate was 5,000 yuan, and 4,000 yuan has already been disbursed. There is still 1,000 yuan outstanding. The project is 80% complete. The disaster situation in Henan is very serious. The province has repeatedly sent documents and telegrams requesting assistance. Because of the shortage of disaster relief funds, the Society only chose to assist Mianchi County and appointed Mr. Feng Yangshan as the disaster relief director. The original allocation was 30,000 yuan. However, it was found that there were more than 20,000 disaster-stricken households, with an average of six people per household, meaning that there were more than 120,000 disaster victims. It was impossible to distribute 30,000 yuan. An additional 25,000 yuan has now been added, bringing the total to 55,000 yuan. It is still necessary to carefully review and make adjustments. (10) Regarding the floods in Huaiyin, Jiangsu Province, and the bandit disasters in Siyang, the Society is jointly working with the Jiangsu Temporary Disaster Relief Association. Because the disaster situation is serious, the Society has added 3,000 yuan to each county. Because epidemics are rampant in the two disaster areas, the Society is sending 5,000 bottles each of Jisheng Dan and Shidi Shui, and 500 boxes of Bao'an Dan to the disaster areas for disaster relief. A philanthropist in Huaian donated 7,500 yuan for farmland and an additional 1,500 yuan, totaling 9,000 yuan, to assist disaster relief in Suqian and Siyang counties. Such acts of kindness and selflessness are worthy of emulation. The Society has published an article in the newspaper to commend them. (11) The Society is currently carrying out disaster relief in nine provinces. In addition to the funds that have already been paid, there are still outstanding payments (list available separately), totaling a shortfall of 152,600 yuan. With such a shortage of disaster relief funds, the Society cannot ignore the disasters that need to be addressed. The only hope is that the Society's comrades and philanthropists will do their best to promote and support the cause, so that disaster victims can survive and blessings will be immeasurable. We who live in safety on the sea, whenever we think of the suffering of the disaster victims, we should each do our best to find ways to provide relief. Saving one more person is one more act of merit. Everyone was deeply moved by this. Member Wang Yao臣 immediately pledged 1,000 yuan for disaster relief in Shaanxi. The director and vice chair were recommended by many of the public; his experience is deep, yet his rope is short; he is afraid of being unequal to the task. With the arrival of such a great disaster, if he waits for enough disaster relief funds to be raised before providing relief, the disaster victims will already be in the ditches. He has no choice but to plan ahead. Last year, he had no choice but to borrow 100,000 yuan, which has been gradually repaid, but now there is another shortfall of 150,000 yuan. He hopes that all his comrades will understand God's great virtue and intention to give life. With such widespread calamities, philanthropists across the country will unite to provide relief, and many people will surely join the Society. The public unanimously agreed. After discussing various internal matters of the Society, the meeting was adjourned with a bell.

First Hearing of the Sino-German Association

The Sino-German Association, aiming to foster Sino-German cultural exchange and promote Sino-German friendship, held its first gathering yesterday (the 6th) at Xinghualou at 7 p.m. Attendees included Chinese representatives such as Cai Yuanpei, Hu Shuhua, Shen Junyi, Xu Yuanfang, and Ma Yinliang from this publication. Second Meeting of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Industry Public Bond Management Committee

Silk factory representatives request flexible measures

Management based on Article 3 of the regulations

The Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Industry Public Bond Management Committee held its second executive committee meeting yesterday at 9 a.m. at the Industry and Commerce Visiting Bureau of the Ministry of Industry on Sanma Road. Attendees included Zheng Hongnian, Vice Minister of Industry; Management Committee members Mu Ouchu, Zou Bingwen, Shen Huachen, Lu Shutang, Chu Huisheng, Qian Fenghao; silk experts Zhou Tingding, Zheng Bijiang, Ge Jingzhong; and Cheng Zhenjun, totaling eleven people. Zheng Hongnian, acting as temporary chairman, recorded the discussion as follows:

Discussion: Regarding the allocation of public bonds, according to Article 3 of the Silk Industry Public Bond Regulations, two-fourths of the total 8 million yuan were originally intended to incentivize silk exports and aid the silk industry, one-fourth for improving silk factory machinery, and one-fourth for improving sericulture. During yesterday's discussion, Shen, Chu, and Qian from the silk factory side suggested that the silk industry's situation has been deteriorating over the past two years, especially this year, with almost all Shanghai factories ceasing operations recently. Therefore, to aid the silk industry, the immediate solution should be to maintain the status quo. While improving the silk industry is also urgent, it should only be discussed after the silk industry stabilizes. They requested that the 2 million yuan for improving machinery be temporarily used to aid the silk industry as an emergency measure. After a lengthy discussion, the chairman deemed the suggestion inappropriate, believing that improvement and aid are separate matters, and the public bond regulations were stipulated by the Legislative Yuan and cannot be illegally altered. Later, Chu Huisheng explained that the silk industry was requesting flexibility, not alteration. As a result, the chairman asked the silk experts to research and determine a plan, with further discussion scheduled for the next, third meeting.

Resolutions: The following resolutions were passed: (1) Ge Jingzhong, Chu Huisheng, and Mu Ouchu were elected as standing committee members. (2) The liaison office was decided to be the staff of the Industry and Commerce Visiting Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, in contact with Guo Bingwen. (3) The detailed rules of procedure will be drafted by Committee Member Mu Ouchu and discussed by the Standing Committee. (4) The public bond allocation plan will be based on the allocation standards stipulated in Article 3 of the public bond regulations, with the committee discussing the plan and submitting a proposal to the ministry for approval. (5) The third executive committee meeting will be held next Monday afternoon. As for the flexible measures requested by the silk factory representatives, it is said that a decision will be made at the next meeting.

Customs Declaration Method for Transporting Native Goods

Must be reported to the Customs at the port of departure

The Jianghai Customs received an order from the Ministry of Finance yesterday stating that merchants transporting native goods with fixed tax receipts from one commercial port to another, passing through foreign ports, or from a commercial port through Dalian to various locations in the three northeastern provinces, must submit a written pledge to the customs at the port of departure at the time of declaration. The pledge must state that the goods being transported are indeed the original goods and have not been altered or replaced. The goods must arrive at the port of destination within three months from the date of declaration. The order instructed compliance and adherence. Upon receiving the order, the Jianghai Customs immediately notified all merchants to comply.

Bookbinding Industry Scheduled to Resume Work Today

Signatures Not Achieved Yesterday

The third strike by workers in the Chinese and foreign bookbinding industry in this city has lasted for nine days. While foreign bookbinding has resumed work, Chinese bookbinding has not yet complied. Signatures were not achieved yesterday. Since the authorities' deadline has passed, the union sent representatives again to persuade the workers, who have agreed to resume work today. The situation yesterday is recorded as follows:

Signatures Not Achieved: Pu Xieji, represented by Pu Fenglai, and Tang Pinji, represented by Kang Aping, whose proposed solutions, after discussions with worker representatives, were opposed by all colleagues. Yesterday, they sent a letter to worker representative Lu Axiang, stating, "We acknowledge the excellent negotiations conducted yesterday between your representatives and us regarding the resumption of work. However, this labor dispute arose from your union's reorganization efforts, and your representatives and we are in private capacities. Therefore, we bear no responsibility for the matters discussed yesterday. If your union is truly sincere about resuming work, please submit a written proposal to our association for legal discussion." Later, worker representative Zhang Jinhong arrived to represent Pu Fenglai, but Pu Fenglai and others refused to sign, and first resumed work. The bookbinding union, to comply with the order, sent maintenance team members again yesterday morning with notices to various workshops to persuade workers, and they have all agreed to resume work today and await a resolution. The East Team included Huang Songhe and Yu A'gen; the South Team included Chen Xiaosong and Pu Xiguang; the West Team included Feng Shaoquan and Lu Jianqiu; the North Team included Chao Guosheng and Shen Changjiang, totaling over twenty people. They returned to the union at 4 p.m., each reporting that workers had agreed to resume work today and await a resolution.

Capitalists Petition: The Bookbinding Industry Association sent representatives Li Guangzu, Zhu Muyun, and others to the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday morning to petition for strict action against illegal strikes. Wang Bing received their report on recent developments and instructed them to follow the authorities' announcements. They then went to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to petition for assistance in maintaining commercial difficulties. Zheng Chengqing received them and agreed to forward the matter to the Social Affairs Bureau for legal review.

Japanese Sailors Suddenly Want to Cooperate with Chinese Sailors

Japanese Seek a Way Out

Not Initially Loving Chinese People

The Japanese Seamen's Union, which has established a Shanghai branch, is a collection of maritime personnel from various shipping companies, mainly composed of lower-ranking sailors. In recent years, the Japanese shipping industry has been facing a downturn, with excessive tonnage and increasing numbers of unemployed sailors. In order to find a way out, the Seamen's Union first established a branch in Hong Kong, welcoming Chinese sailors to join in order to achieve the internationalization of maritime personnel. Recently, with the decline in Japanese shipping operations, Japanese sailors realized that they could not find a new way out without uniting with Chinese sailors. Therefore, they decided to send personnel to Shanghai to prepare for the establishment of a Shanghai branch of the Japanese Seamen's Union, in cooperation with a portion of the Chinese sailors of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, to form a united front. This is currently being organized.

Decision to Make Demands: After the Japanese and Chinese sailors cooperate and unite, they have decided to make demands of the British and Japanese shipping companies. Generally, at a time when gold prices are soaring and business is depressed, the British and Japanese shipping companies should employ Chinese sailors for the lower-ranking positions on all ships, except for the senior officers. This would not only save the huge expenditure of paying salaries in gold coins but also because Chinese sailors are better at the work than sailors from other countries. This action by the Japanese is not initially to find a way out for Chinese sailors. They know that the number of Chinese sailors with specialized maritime skills is insufficient. They are using the name of Chinese sailors' low salaries and excellent work to, in reality, encourage European countries to employ more Japanese sailors as crew members in the future.

Sanbei Company's Changan Steamer Runs Aground on Yangtze River

The stranded Sanbei Company Yangtze River steamer Changan was originally planning to go to Changsha, Hunan after going to Shashi from Shanghai. On the afternoon of the 3rd of this month, at 9:00 p.m., while traveling to the river surface about 20 miles away from Jianli, the water level was sharply falling. The ship ran aground on a shoal, and the hull was deeply mired in the sand.

Towing: On the second day after being stranded, the water level was only eight feet, and the bottom of the ship was wrapped in the sand. While considering towing, the Ningshao Company's Yongxing steamer also happened to be passing by after sailing from Hankou. Seeing the Changan stranded, it tried to tow it, but the force was insufficient due to the shallow water, so it stopped towing and sent a telegram to Shanghai to report and seek a solution.

Waiting for the Tide: According to a telegram from Hankou yesterday, the water level in Jianli is only eight meters, making navigation very difficult. A slight mishap could lead to disaster. The area where the Changan is stranded is also only eight feet deep, making it impossible for ships with deeper drafts to approach and tow. It is now necessary to wait for the tide to rise to ten feet before towing can be attempted. It is not yet known whether the bottom of the Changan has been damaged and it will be necessary to wait for the tide to rise and tow it out before inspecting it.

Minghe Steamer Abandoned and Not Salvaged

The entire ship sank into the sand

The crew was rescued by the Fengpu

After the Sanbei Company's Minghe steamer ran aground on a reef at Peacock Port in Beihai Prefecture, Saisui Prefecture last month, the bureau sent the Fengpu steamer to rescue it. It took almost a month until yesterday, when a telegram was received from Suisui Prefecture stating that after the Minghe steamer ran aground on the reef, it was surrounded by sand and mud due to the impact of the tide. It is now impossible to tow it, and even the Fengpu steamer can only anchor three thousand feet away from the Minghe and cannot get any closer. Therefore, after inspection by the technicians, it can only be completely abandoned and not salvaged. The small sampan boats have now begun to transfer the Minghe's crew and sailors to safety, and the parts of the ship that can be disassembled are also being loaded onto the Fengpu steamer for transport back to Shanghai. The Minghe steamer is a top-notch ship of the Sanbei Company, valued at over 400,000 yuan, with a load capacity of over 2,000 tons and covered by Ping An marine insurance. This complete loss will amount to at least 400,000 yuan, but it will be borne by the insurance company.

Post Office Limits Domestic Parcel Weight

Increased from 10 kg to 20 kg

The Shanghai Post Office stated that the weight limit for domestic parcels has now been increased from 10 kg to 20 kg. For parcels sent to and from places not connected by domestic ships and trains, the size limit has also been changed to be the same as those sent to and from places connected by ships and trains. This change will be implemented on a trial basis for one year. Details can be inquired at various post offices.

This is truly the glory of the national goods industry and the pride of the Chinese nation.

News from Various Labor Unions

Declaration by Various Labor Unions in the Fifth District Against the Atrocities of American Sailors: It is said that there must be no docile people in a country of rapists. American imperialists have always used the guise of a civilized country to appeal to the world, but in reality, their weaknesses are exposed and they cannot defend themselves. It is a self-deception that the world already agrees upon. Recently, tragic cases have emerged one after another in Shanghai, a small place. Since the shooting of Gu Jingen by American sailors, there have been continuous incidents of American sailors committing violence while drunk, American sailors pushing people into the Huangpu River, and American sailors wielding knives to kill people, causing death or injury and splattering blood. Public opinion is spreading and shocking the world. At this time, our country is abolishing unequal treaties, yet the imperialists dare to be so rampant, acting lawlessly within our country's territory. The so-called army of a self-proclaimed civilized country openly holds knives to kill people, what will uncivilized countries do? Now, the dead cannot be revived, the injured are gasping for breath, negotiations have not yet been successful, the dead drink their hatred in the afterlife, and the injured pillow their grievances. What could be more heartbreaking than this? It concerns the survival of the nation. Punishing the perpetrators and providing compensation are only temporary solutions. Recovering extraterritoriality is the only way to eliminate the harm permanently. Preserving the country and seeking survival is a clear and ancient teaching. May all our compatriots in the country share this conviction. (The following omitted) Shanghai Fifth District Cigarette Industry Union, Fifth District Shipbuilding Industry Union, Fifth District Paper Industry Union, Fifth District Stevedoring Union, Fifth District Match Industry Union, Fifth District Altar Industry Union, Fifth District Woodworking Industry Union, Fifth District Garment Union, Fifth District Yellow Wine Production Union, Fifth District Basket Carrier Union, Fifth District Casing Slice Union, Fifth District Civil Ship Repair Union, etc. declare.

The Pharmaceutical Trade Union held its fourth board of directors and supervisors meeting yesterday. Chairman Zhao Zhenhui conducted the ceremony as usual. After the chairman reported the purpose, various cases were discussed: (1) The accountant of this union has been ill for a long time, causing the financial report to be delayed for several months. He is unable to continue to be responsible and requests to resign. How should this case be handled? It was resolved that since the director is unable to perform his duties due to illness, his resignation is approved. Ye Baozhong is hereby appointed as the accountant. All previous financial reports shall be handled by Ye Baozhong in conjunction with the former director and completed before June 20th. Approved. (2) How should the membership fees solicited by the Lianyi Society, an affiliated group of this union, be handled this time? It was resolved that after the funds are collected, they will be deposited into the Ningbo Commercial Bank, stamped with the seal of this union. The passbook shall be kept by the accounting department. If there is a special purpose, it shall be proposed by the general affairs department and approved by the meeting before it can be withdrawn. (3) Some workers in a certain shop have not joined the union and there is no adequate solution. Doubts have arisen among the members. How should this be handled? It was resolved: A. The names of the workers in the shop who have not joined the union will be listed, and the circumstances of their undermining of the labor movement and their past history will be printed in a notice to the members. B. Advertisements will be published in various newspapers to announce the various crimes of the workers and that the old membership cards are invalid. In the future, the union will not accept any labor disputes. C. The various bad deeds and names of the workers will be engraved on wooden plaques and hung in the union for public viewing as a permanent reminder. D. (Confidential) (4) How should Qi Jinxian's letter requesting restoration of membership be handled? It was resolved to handle it according to the previous case. As a temporary motion, Zhao Zhenhui mentioned that the Daily News reported that the Social Affairs Bureau ordered unemployed members of all unions to register. Should unemployed members of this union be notified to go and register? Please decide publicly. It was resolved that notices will be distributed, limiting the time for unemployed members to go to the Social Affairs Bureau to register. Approved. Comrade Fang Qingjian proposed that the members recruited by Lianyi Society this time have not been adequately trained. Should they be summoned regularly? It was decided to summon the members to the union for training at 1:00 PM on the 12th of this month. Furthermore, it has been repeatedly reported by a large number of members that certain capitalists are engaging in extensive activities to attack this union. Should this union prepare accordingly or announce the past crimes of inciting capitalists and creating a disturbance? Please decide publicly. It was resolved to announce the crimes. Meeting adjourned.

Letter Received

To the editor: Today (6th), your newspaper published a report on the resolution of the bookbinding industry turmoil, which is slightly inconsistent with the facts. On the morning of June 5th, the laborers Zhang Jinhong, Zhang Haosheng, and I had a private conversation at the Wanshang Teahouse in Xinzha Bridge, which was not a formal meeting. At that time, it was stated that we would report to our union based on personal opinions. If a resolution could be reached, a formal signature would be required to be effective. Now, reading the newspaper's report that an agreement had been reached is not in line with the facts. I hereby declare this and request that your newspaper make a correction to clarify the truth. Respectfully, Pu Fenglai from Pudong sends this message to the chief editor of the Shenbao. May 6th.
